*****HOW IT WORKS AND WHAT TO EXPECT.*****

The way it works is as follows they ask that you give them 90 days to find you a place which the point of the contract and it cannot be terminated until after the 90 days. They collect your personal information including pay stubs for proof of income. They will also require to sign a form to run your credit which will cost $50 which is part of the 200 dollar fee they charge. Then they will give you a list of properties that meets your budget and desire locations which then they will ask you to go check out those properties and pick 3 that you like and let them know so they can schedule a viewing and if you like the apartment you then take an application fill it out to them and send to them they can do the rest. They have new listings every Wednesday but you can only get a copy of those new listings thru fax.

What your really getting for $200 is a broker office who will schedule viewing appointments, submit your application, and get you a list of properties that meet your budget and desires location. However, they don't have any connections with any of the properties and cannot negotiate a better deal for you since they get their properties from the MLS.

***** How is this for ****
If your someone who doesn't want to searching for a apartments and want someone to submit your paper work and schedule viewings for you then this is for you.</text>< username>

<date>1520967933066<//date><review>SCAM ALERT!

This place is BAD news. First, beware of a place that tells you cash or money order only- you're not getting your money back once it's in their hands. Second, before you walk out the door, they insist that you sign a contract saying that they've fulfilled their minimum of giving you at least three potential properties that fit your criteria; that way, if you manage to find a way to get your refund (highly unlikely), it'll be much less than the amount you originally gave them.

They're not legitimate. They pull all kinds of rental listings off the Internet without bothering to check if they're real, like craigslist, so a bunch of stuff they give you is completely fake.

The problem is they have you sign all kinds of contracts and paperwork so that you can't take them to court. What they're doing is not illegal, just highly unethical. But they don't care whom they rip off, as long as they get the money. We wanted to stay at the hotel and enjoy the amenities, since we're members, finally away for our one trip, and our young kid was going to lose it since it was late and we were hungry. So we told them we'd come back in 15-20 minutes. When we came back, they were seating people immediately without reservations. We were seated and ignored. The person who seated us said they'd bring a high chair. They never came back. No one did. Not for drinks, nothing. Even though we knew it was late and it would upset our kid, we had no choice but to leave. The moment we stood up, our table was cleared.

<Resp>None</Resp><pictures>None</pictures>< Text>
I hiked this in snow. It was incredibly beautiful. It would take a poet to do the view at the top justice.

Be VERY careful when there's ice. Things get very slippery, especially near the summit. It would be very easy to slip and careen off the side to your death, so hold fast to the handrails near the top and take it slowly and surely.

There's no signal on T-Mobile for most of the hike, but the summit had signal, in case you need to make an emergency call.</Text>

<user_id>117422070604730894133<//user_id>< Review>
We arrived at 830 am.  You must park across the street and pay $10 for parking.  The trail is absolutely beautiful and there was plenty of shade as the brush is very tall on both sides.  It's 2 miles to the top, and fairly easy trail.  We saw 2 snakes but both were getting out of our way. The view at the top is amazing, overlooking miles and miles all the way around.  The top is the best part, be sure to climb up the steps to the top.  We had a snack, took pictures and headed down the hill.  It's an easy walk down.  I love this hike it was fast and easy for us. I was back in San Diego at noon.<//Review>

< text>
In short, there are many items that need to be resolved for this place to stay in business. The quality of their product will make me a repeat customer, but the frequency of my visits will depend on their ability to overcome their many flaws.

My family visited twice on opening day--once at noon and again at 6:30PM. In both cases, there were less than six people in line and we waited over 20 minutes each time to just place our order. After ordering the first time, our drink order was fulfilled in under 5 minutes. During our evening visit, we waited 15 minutes for our ice cream after ordering. The wait time the second time around was due to the lack of employees, and one person playing "one man band" behind the counter (answering questions from both customers and the untrained cashier, giving samples, scooping ice cream, calling out orders, and running cups back and forth from the register to the kitchen).

The things that need to change ASAP and shouldn't cost the company significant dollars:
- Two employees (cashier and "runner") are not enough to take care of customers. Have more staff behind the counter to answer questions, provide ice cream samples, and start taking drink/ice cream orders before customers reach the cashier. During slower hours, these employees can also clean the bathrooms, empty trash, and interact with customers (rather than just apologize for taking so long). Doing the little things goes a long way for the customer experience.
- Train your cashiers on how to use the POS system properly. This creates a large bottleneck.
- Have your drink stickers print directly to the kitchen area. Currently, the labels print at the cashier, they have to put the labels on cups, and then have them run them to the kitchen window (about 15-20 feet away).

Changes that would be nice:
- If things remain busy, run two cash registers.
- Widen the section for those standing in line. There is currently very narrow standing room and it would be a nightmare for someone with claustrophobia or young kids.
- Open earlier. People may not want ice cream at 10:00am, but they will definitely would drink boba tea at that time.
- Stay open later (til 9:00 or 10:00pm?). Your most likely demographic is 15-30 year olds---think about it. Most boba shops in the area stay open until 9-11pm on weeknights
- Add a Vietnamese Iced Coffee DRINK to the menu. The VIC ice cream is awesome... but I'd come back 3x a week if there was a drink to go with it.
- Don't charge customers extra for adding a regular boba. "Boba" is in your name, yet you add an up-charge when people want it in their drink. Specialty add-ins deserve to be marked up.
- Add a customer loyalty program to reward repeat visitors.
- Don't raise your drink prices. Currently Sweet Lab is on the high end of pricing for their teas. Most of your competitors are charging $2.75-3.50 for regular sized milk tea (boba included) with an extra $0.50-0.75 if they are ordering a larger size.
- Run regular specials. This can encourage new customers to come in and get returning customers to try new drinks/ice creams.

I plan to go again in the next several days and hopefully will be able to change my review for the better. With the right changes, this local business should be able to thrive!<//text>

<review>The baked goods merchandised in this bakery‚Äôs display case will no doubt tantalize your senses.

Speaking from experience.

This was my first visit, and I knew I was in for a treat when at a 10 a.m. on a Friday there was a line out the door. Lines are usually a promising sign of a good business. And the experience was worth the wait.

Indeed, this bakery serves a diverse selection of upscale pastries and other gastronomic delights.

On your visit you can expect to see huge cookies with eclectic and traditional flavors, croissants, scones, brioche, muffins, and more.

In addition to fresh baked bread there are paninis and other sandwiches available for lunch.

In spite of all that above, I have only had the Quiche of The Day. It was ham, egg, and cheddar cheese, and it was good. IMO, it would have been much better hot or at least lukewarm, but instead it was served at room temperature.

The lady taking my order said they weren‚Äôt able to heat it due to COVID-19.

Aside from that, good experience.
The prices can be on the dear side, as in ‚Äúoh dear!‚Äù.
So don‚Äôt be surprised if a huge cookie or a single slice of quiche cost  $6.00.

All in all, 4.4 stars out of 5, or said another way, an 88 out of 100.

Final thought and tip.

Whatever your choice, I hope you enjoy.

<user>109514665259259475780<//user><user_name>Butch Butler<//user_name><date>1612260481764< /date><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
I've been to this bakery several times. I love their olive oil and olives twist pastry. I try to get it every time I visit if it isn't sold out. On weekends there is usually a line and currently during COVID-19, they limit 6 customers at a time in the store. They have a small parking lot that can accommodate less than 10 cars, otherwise there is metered parking near by. On our latest visit on a Saturday at 10am, we waited 20 minutes to get inside. It's true that their pastries do not have prices in the store but it can be viewed on their website. In general they are between $4-$5 each. I've never had any bad customer service experience with any of the employees. Their selection is big from cookies, to cakes, pastries, and sandwiches. On occasion they will have seasonal items. Their eggnog kouign amann is amazing and this is coming from someone who doesn't like to drink eggnog.<//Review>

< text>
Best bread in SF! Love the density and tartness of the multigrain loaf. So sweet that they will sell you a half loaf too (just ask!). Cookies are the BOMB (the captain crunch cookie is eerily true to taste, but with all the buttery chewy goodness of a cookie :)).

Four stars because the coffee is a little acidic for my taste and the pastries do not live up to their aesthetics (too doughy/bready for me, I like flaky pastry). The much hyped cardamom bun had lovely filling and is a creative idea, but the dough prevented me from enjoying it. Toasts are a cute idea, but on bread that is already darkly browned, I found my fig ricotta toast to be too singed to really savor.

Have not tried the gargantuan sandwiches, salads, or cakes... they‚Äôre on the list!<//text>

< Review>
Wonderful bakery offering a huge variety of baked goods. Fantastic pastries, cookies, and other sweets. They also have a great assortment of fresh breads and also offer food items like breakfast sandwiches which are very generous and delicious.
The location is not very conspicuous and the outside of the bakery doesn‚Äôt have a lot of signage. I actually confused it for an old KFC when I first moved to the neighborhood because of an old awning on the side. But I think that people who live nearby are becoming more aware of it and I would definitely recommend trying any of their items. It would be worth the trip.
The earlier you get there, the better!< /Review>

<gmapID>0x808580b9c8e6d781:0xc66d155748e1a74b< /gmapID>< Review>
This is a delightful bakery. Not only are their basic croissants and breads top notch, they also are very creative with flavors, both savory and sweet. A croissant dough tart with carrots and goat cheese and a hint of curry and thyme suggests a Thanksgiving flavor. Their citrus tart isn't just straightforward lemon with meringue, it also has a hint of raspberry, grapefruit, and rosemary in the crust, which worked amazingly well together. The avocado toast is so much more than just avocado. I would rate this as one of the 3 best bakeries in SF. The only downside is not much room to sit down and eat, hopefully it's a nice day and you can eat your pastries in the park across the street.<//Review>

I have been here 4 times. The croissants are excellent, perfect. The choices of breads, great--I have tried three different kinds and they are also delicious and excellent. < Review>
Stopped by on a Saturday afternoon, not too many people so line wasn't too long. They had a variety of baked goods and to go lunches. For some reason the prices were not posted so it was hard to know how much things cost. The space itself is fairly small, like it was meant to be a to go kind of place, not a place to sit and enjoy coffee and pastries.

We got 4 pastry items, all of which were ok, not bad, not great. For close to $19 tho, we felt it was overpriced and didn't deserve another visit. I'd instead visit Japantown 2 blocks away where for $19 you could almost get a sit-down meal for 2.<//Review>
